Answer: Try using [this](https://github.com/google-corporate-labs/universal-sentence-encoder) library for translating sentences, it's really good at handling languages like Hindi with its own grammar rules.

Here's a simple code snippet on how to use it.

\begin{code}
from google_corporate_labs import sentence_encoder as se
import numpy as np
import tensorflow as tf

# Create an input sentence
sentences = ["I am feeling great today."]

# Use Universal Sentence Encoder (USE) to encode each sentence into vectors
encodings = se.encode(sentences)

# Plot the encoded sentences
plt.figure()
for idx, sentence in enumerate(sentences):
    plt.plot(np.array([1, encodings[idx].values]), 'b')
plt.show()
\end{code}</s>

Comment: It's a common idiomatic expression, but it's not a proverb and doesn't have any specific meaning other than what you would expect based on the individual words.

Answer: The phrase "sixth incident" is an example of a [collocation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collocation), i.e., a group of words that are frequently found together. In this case, "sixth" is used as an adjective modifying "incident."

In general, collocations don't necessarily have fixed meanings or implications.</s>
[Actual English]: This is the seventh incident in the past few days.

var text = "If you tell the truth about land, it is much worse situation.";

console.log(translated);
\end{code}

### [1436. इंजन की क्षमता](https://leetcode.com/problems/engine-power/)

#### Solution

```cpp
// O(n)
class Solution {
public:
    int enginePower(vector<int>& fuel, vector<int>& power) {
        int n = fuel.size();
        if (n == 0 || power.empty()) return -1;
        
        int ans = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {
            if (fuel[i] <= 0 && power[i] >= 0) continue;
            
            int left = 0;
            for (int j = 0; j < i; ++j) {
                left += fuel[j];
                if (left >= power[j]) break;
            }
            
            ans += left;
        }
        
        return ans;
    }
};
```

Answer: You can use Regex to do it in one line:

\begin{code}
var match = Regex.Match(text, @"(?<=\[Hindi])(.*?)(?=\[English])");
if (match.Success)
    Console.WriteLine(match.Groups["1"].Value);
else
    Console.WriteLine("No match found.");
\end{code}</s>

import requests
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup as bs

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: तेज रफ्तार जीप ट्रक के पिछले हिस्से में जा घुसी। 
[English]:  The speeding truck got stuck in the back of the jeep.
\end{blockquote}

The first sentence means that the jeep is stuck behind a truck which is moving fast (in Hindi, it means "speeding").

The second sentence means that the truck is going so fast that it has already reached the back part of the jeep and stopped there.

Comment: Thank you very much for your answer. But I'm confused about the usage of the word 'हिस्से'. Is this the right translation?

Comment: @SagarKulkarni Yes, it is correct.</s>
[Actual English]: The speeding jeep collided with the back of truck.
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: उसका अगला हिस्सा बुरी तरह क्षतिग्रस्त हो गया। 
[English]:  His next step was disastrous.

### Explanation:
In this example, the word "step" has been translated into both "उसका अगला हिस्सा" and "next step". This is because in Hindi there are two words that mean "step", but they have different connotations depending on context. The first word, "हिस्सा", means a physical action or movement (e.g., walking), while the second word, "अगला", means something that comes after another thing in time or sequence (e.g., next). Therefore, when translating from Hindi to English we must choose between these two possible translations based on their respective meanings within each language. In this case we chose "his next step" because it better captures what happened with regards to timing rather than just describing an action without any reference point in space-time continuum; otherwise one could interpret this sentence as saying "his last step" instead which would be incorrect since he took more than one step before reaching his destination!
</s>

Answer: Try this:

\begin{code}
import re

text = 'शुक्रवार को दरोगा के शव को पुलिस लाइन में सलामी दी गई।'

re_pattern = r'\b([A-Za-z]{3})\w+,\s*(?:\d{4})'

matches = re.finditer(re_pattern, text)
for match in matches:
    print('{0}: {1}'.format(match.group(), match.start()))
\end{code}</s>

\strong{Edit:} I found the following sentence in a book by Jawaharlal Nehru (The Discovery of India, p.59):

\begin{blockquote}
There is a beautiful and ancient story about a king who had a dream that he would die if his son did not succeed him. He asked his ministers what they thought of it. One said that it meant that his son would succeed him; another said that it meant that his son would kill him; but a third minister said that the king's death was certain, because he had forgotten to fast before going to sleep. The king did not know which interpretation to follow, so he decided to ask an old man who lived near the palace. The old man told him that he should fast for three days, after which the king would die.
\end{blockquote}

Comment: @user66974 I think the OP's question refers to the verb "lie" as a transitive verb.

Comment: I think the same thing. I don't see how "lie" could be used here without a direct object.

Answer: This is a case where "lie" can mean both "to recline" and "to rest or remain in a particular position". It seems like the author has used the second meaning in this context.

Comment: Are you sure that you want to translate "business" as "bikri"?

Answer: You have a number of issues here, so let me go through them one by one.

Firstly, your text contains some very strange characters which are not valid in English (or any other Western European language). For example, there is an 'ए' character and a 'ई'. These are not part of any Western alphabet, and so Google Translate does not know what they mean.

Secondly, even if these characters were valid, they would still be wrong because they are transliterations into Devanagari script. This is not the same thing as translation. The correct way to write 'business' in Hindi is व्यापार.

Thirdly, even if you could get past all those problems, you should realise that you don't need to use a translation tool for this kind of thing. If you really want to translate something like this, then you need to do it yourself, by learning how to speak/write Hindi. There are plenty of resources available online, including [this](https://www.google.co.uk/url?sa=t&rct=j&q=&esrc=s&source=web&cd=1&cad=rja&uact=8&ved=0ahUKEwjp4KvVp9PLAhXGKY8KHWdRBxIQFgggMAE&url=http%3A%2F%2Flearn-hindi.org%2Flessons%2Fhindi-alphabet%2F&usg=AFQjCNE6aLJZmNy77Dk-e_M8nS0iO7Z9jA) one, which includes audio clips of people speaking in Hindi.</s>
[Actual English]: We are expecting the sales of diamonds to go up by 25 percent this year.
==================================================

[English]:  Last year’s gold prices were lower than this year. Still, people are buying more gold this time. 

##### Expected Output
```
Last year's gold price was lower than this year's. But still, people are buying more gold this time.
```
</s>

Comment: I think you've got the right answer here but there are some minor issues with your translation. The first one is that 'कर्म करना' means 'to do work', so it should be translated as 'doing something'. Secondly, 'निलंबित करना' doesn't mean 'to make someone helpless', rather it just means 'to dismiss someone'. You could translate it as 'dismissed him/her'. Finally, the word 'करा' (करना) is not used for 'to say' in Hindi, rather it is only used for 'to do' or 'to make'. So you can use 'said' instead of 'made them say'.

Answer: I have found an alternative translation on [WordReference](https://www.wordreference.com/indianenglish/kisi+karanahin):

\begin{blockquote}
He had made him say the words "I am guilty"
\end{blockquote}</s>
[Actual English]: He said that on the 4th of July he had complained about the Secretary and the Chief and as a result the Chief suspended him.

[English]:  They also gave evidence that the Panchayati Raj President was working against the orders of the Chief.

#### 2017

In 2017, the Supreme Court ordered the Government of India to pay Rs 1 lakh compensation to each of the five petitioners who had challenged the appointment of Justice K M Joseph as a judge of the Supreme Court on 31 August 2016 by President Pranab Mukherjee. The order was given by Chief Justice J S Khehar and Justices D Y Chandrachud and L Nageswara Rao.

The court said that the government had violated the fundamental rights of the petitioners under Article 14 (right to equality) and Article 21 (right to life and personal liberty).

The Supreme Court also asked the Centre to appoint two judges to the top court before 3 October 2017.

### 2018

On 25 January 2018, the Supreme Court directed the Centre to fill up four vacancies in the Supreme Court by 31 March 2018.

On 29 May 2018, the Supreme Court ruled that the collegium system is constitutional and valid. The court also made it clear that it is for the executive to decide whether or not to accept the recommendations of the collegium.

On 26 July 2018, the Supreme Court refused to stay the notification issued by the Ministry of Personnel, Public Grievances and Pensions appointing 42 additional judges to various high courts. The court also dismissed the plea filed by senior advocate Indira Jaising seeking an independent probe into the alleged irregularities in the process of selection of judicial officers.

On 11 September 2018, the Supreme Court appointed former Chief Justice of Patna High Court Rajendra Menon as the next chief justice of Madras High Court. He will replace Justice Vijaya Kamlesh Tahilramani, whose term ends on 11 November 2018.

On 18 December 2018, the Supreme Court rejected the Centre's request

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: लोगों को प्रेरित करते हुए कहा कि यदि कोई अधिकारी या कर्मचारी किसी भी काम के लिए रिश्वत की मांग करता है तो उसकी शिकायत विजिलेंस विभाग से की जा सकती है। 
[English]:  It is clarified that if any officer or employee of the State Government/Government Department makes a demand for redressal of any grievance, then such grievance can be made to the Department.
— Ministry of Law and Justice (@MOLIndia) September 24, 2019
The statement comes after reports emerged on social media alleging that government officials were charging citizens Rs 500-Rs 2,000 to help them in filing complaints with authorities.
According to an official at the Delhi Grievances Redressal Authority (DGRA), the law mandates that every department should have a dedicated email address to which people can send their grievances. “If you are not able to find the address online, please write to us,” he said. “We will get back to you.”
The DGRA was set up under the Delhi Government’s Right to Services Act, 2015, which provides for timely delivery of services by all public authorities within the national capital. The law also requires each department to appoint one nodal officer who is responsible for ensuring the delivery of services.
“People often approach us with complaints about officers who charge money for filing their grievances,” the official added. “However, we do not have any mechanism to take action against such officials as they don’t fall under our jurisdiction.”
He further explained that while the DGRA has the power to issue directions to public authorities regarding the provision of services, it cannot take action against individual officers.
The DGRA website lists several helplines where people can register their complaints, including one specifically for those seeking assistance in filing grievances. However, some users have expressed frustration over the lack of information available on the site.
In response to the criticism, the DGRA issued a statement on Twitter saying that it would soon launch a mobile app that would allow people to track the status of their complaints. “We are working hard to make sure that everyone gets the service they deserve,” the tweet read.
While the move towards digitisation is welcome, many users remain concerned about the potential for abuse of the system. One user pointed out that even if the app is successful in reducing corruption, there is still no guarantee that the public servants using it will actually deliver on their promises.

words = sentence.split()
print(words)
for w in words:
    print(w)

#print(re.findall('\d+', sentence))
#print(word_tokenize(sentence))
\end{code}

Answer: You can use [Regex](https://docs.python.org/3/library/re.html).

For example, you can match the number with `\d+` and the text after that with `.*`:

### 50. कुछ भी नहीं है जो तुम्हें अपने ही होने पर नहीं होता।
Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: 
1. कुछ भी नहीं है जो तुम्हें अपने ही होने पर नहीं होता। 
2. There is nothing that will not happen to you, if it happens to you.
3. There is no such thing which will not happen to you, even if it happens to you.
4. There is nothing that will not happen to you, just because it happened to you.

```python
import nltk
from nltk import word_tokenize, sent_tokenize, pos_tag

sentences = [line.strip() for line in open("data/hindi-to-english.txt", encoding="utf8")]

def tokenize(sentence):
    return word_tokenize(sent_tokenize(pos_tag(sentence)))

for sentence in sentences:
    print(tokenize(sentence))
```
</s>

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: उसके परिवार की स्थिति ठीक नहीं होने के कारण इसे हम रख रहे हैं। 
[English]:  We have kept him in our family because of the condition of his family.

\end{blockquote}

The translation is not literal, but I think it conveys the meaning of the sentence quite well.

Answer: \begin{itemize}
\item \em{in order to} can be used with a verb in the passive voice or a verb that does not take an object.
\item The present perfect continuous tense indicates that something has been happening over time.
\end{itemize}

\strong{Example:}

\begin{blockquote}

We are keeping him in order to improve his situation.
\end{blockquote}</s>
[Actual English]: As her family's situation is not so good, we are taking care of her.

Answer: The word \em{[dead](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dead#Verb)} is a [transitive verb](http://www.oxforddictionaries.com/definition/english/transitive). \begin{blockquote}
The doctors declared Ganga Devi dead of heart attack.
\end{blockquote}</s>

BJP has announced the names of 135 candidates for the first phase of UP Assembly Elections on Monday. The party has decided to give tickets to 20 women and 11 Muslims out of these 135 candidates.
Among them, two Dalit leaders are also being fielded from Ambedkar Nagar and Ballia districts respectively.
In this way, BJP is going to contest in all the 78 seats of the first phase. Earlier, on Sunday, the party had declared the name of its candidate for the second phase.</s>
[Actual English]: As per the list issued by the BJP, Ishwardas Rohani from Cant, Sharad Jain from the North-Centre, Aanchal Sonkar from the East, Ajay Vishnoi from Paatan- Majhauli and Pratibha Singh from Bargi have been included.
==================================================

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: उन्होंने जहां एक बार यह कहा कि यदि यह ऑपरेशन सेना करती तो सच अब तक सामने आ चुका होता। 
[English]:  He said that if the Operation Thunderbolt had been done by the Indian Army, it would have become a fact now.

### The usage of होता in the sentence

The word होता is used as a passive participle of the verb होना (to happen) and the word होता has the meaning "become" or "turn into". So this sentence means that he says that if the Operation Thunderbolt was done by the Indian army, then it would have turned into a fact.</s>
[Actual English]: Once he said that if this operation was being undertaken by the army, the truth would have been known already.

##### Explanation:

In this sentence, the word "शुरू" is used in a sense of 'started'. In the given context, it should be translated as "started".

### Sentence No. 1403 - 
फिर भी सच्ची तौर पर इनका अधिकार का पालन नहीं कर पाया था।

The result is correct, but I want the translation to be done for all the sentences in the text.

Comment: You should look into using a [translation library](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/20618754/how-to-translate-a-text-in-python).

Answer: There are many libraries available that can help you translate your text. Here's an example with [GoogleTranslate](https://pypi.org/project/googletranslator/)

\begin{code}
from googletrans import GoogleTranslator

translator = GoogleTranslator()

for sentence in sentences:
    print(f"From {sentence['language']}: {sentence['text']}")
    translated_sentence = translator.translate(sentence['text'], src='en', dest=sentence['target'])
    print(f"To {sentence['target']}: {translated_sentence}")
\end{code}</s>
[Actual English]: We have chosen some pictures from Gujarat on this occasion.

[English]:  The officials were promoted to the level of Joint Secretary in the CVC itself, even before their probation period was over. 

### Probation Period and Promotion

A probationary officer is a newly recruited government official who has completed his or her graduate degree (Masters) but not yet inducted into service. A probationer's appointment may be terminated by the appointing authority if he/she does not complete the probationary period satisfactorily.

In India, all government servants are appointed on a probation for a specified period, which varies according to the nature of the post and the grade of the employee. During this period, they are under close supervision of an immediate superior officer and are liable to dismissal at any time during the period of probation without assigning any reason. If the probationary period is not extended, the appointee becomes permanent. In case of non-completion of the probationary period, the Government servant is deemed to have resigned from service.

A probationary officer is generally appointed on contract basis. The appointment letter issued to such employees clearly states that it is subject to satisfactory completion of the prescribed probationary period.

The probationary period for officers is normally three years. For the posts below the rank of Assistant Director, the probationary period is two years.

### Permanent Status

If the probationary period is completed satisfactorily, then the probationary officer becomes a permanent employee. He/She can also be given a regular promotion after completing certain number of years of service.

### Appointment on Deputation Basis

Sometimes, the probationary officer is sent to work with other departments on deputation basis. This happens when there is no vacancy available in the department where he/she wants to work.

## See also

* Apprenticeship
* Graduate trainee</s>

### 2015

In 2015, a man named Mohammad Ajmal was killed in police custody and the court had ordered the CBI to investigate the matter. However, his family alleged that the CBI has not made any progress in the investigation. They said that the police are trying to cover up the case by threatening them with false cases. In response, the Delhi Police issued an order stating that they will take strict action against anyone who spreads rumors or creates panic among people through social media platforms such as Facebook or Twitter.

### 2016

In January 2016, a man named Sandeep Singh died while being treated at a hospital after he was shot by police during a protest over the death of another person who had been detained for questioning about his involvement in drug trafficking. His family members accused the police of killing him because they were afraid of what would happen if he told them where he got drugs from.

### 2017

In June 2017, a man named Gurpreet Singh was arrested by Punjab Police on charges of terrorism and murder. He was then taken into custody by Delhi Police when they found out that he had fled from Punjab to avoid arrest. His wife said that her husband had gone missing since February 2017 and she did not know where he was until she saw news reports about his arrest on television. She also claimed that there was no evidence linking him to any crime except for some unsubstantiated claims made by police officers during interrogation sessions with him at their office premises in New Delhi which led to his arrest without any warrant or summons being served upon him first beforehand according to Indian law regarding arrests under Section 41A(2) CrPC (Criminal Procedure Code).

### 2018

In March 2018, a man named Navdeep Singh was arrested by Delhi Police for allegedly assaulting two policemen during an anti-corruption protest. He later died in custody due to "cardiac arrest". His body was cremated without informing his family members or conducting an autopsy report.

[English]: 
I had protested against the increase in fees two years ago too, by sitting on roads and showing my anger. After that, the fees were reduced a little.

### Explanation of translation

1. वर्ष (Year) - The word 'year' is used for a calendar year. It can also be translated as 'annual'.
2. पहले (Earlier) - This means 'before', 'prior to', or 'in advance of'.
3. भी (Also) - This means 'also', 'as well', or 'too'.
4. फीस (Fees) - Fees are charges paid for using services. In this case, it refers to tuition fees.
5. बढ़ाने (Increase) - This means 'to make bigger' or 'to grow larger'.
6. विरोध (Opposition) - This means 'resistance', 'objection', or 'protest'.
7. अभिभावकों (Protesters) - These people are protesting against something.
8. सड़कों (Roads) - Roads are a place where cars travel.
9. उतर (Sit) - To sit somewhere means to be seated at that location.
10. रोष (Anger) - Anger is a strong feeling of displeasure and antagonism.
11. प्रदर्शन (Demonstration) - A demonstration is an organized public event where participants show their support for a cause.
12. फीसों (Fees) - Fees are charges paid for using services. In this case, it refers to tuition fees.
13. थोड़ा (Little) - This means 'a small amount', 'not much', or 'barely any'.

Comment: Welcome to SO! Can you please add a bit more information about your code?

Answer: \begin{blockquote}
I want to get the translation of a particular word. For example if I have the following sentence :

"Translate from Hindi to English:  [Hindi]: प्रमुख ने कहा कि सरकारी कार्य में पारदर्शिता रखकर विकास कार्य को आगे बढ़ाने की जरूरत है।  [English]: The Chief Minister said that in government work, priority should be given to maintaining public image and taking the development work forward."
\end{blockquote}

If you have the sentences, then it is simple. You can use regex with a look-ahead and a look-behind assertion.

\strong{Demo:} https://regex101.com/r/K3FgvP/1

\begin{code}
(?<=[^[:space:]])([^\s]+)([^[:space:]]+)
\end{code}

This pattern matches a space followed by one or more characters that are not spaces and another space followed by one or more characters that are not spaces. Then, group 2 captures the text between the first two spaces. Group 1 captures everything else (except for the first and last character).

\section{[Python demo](https://ideone.com/U69mzx):}

\begin{code}
import re

sentence = "Translate from Hindi to English:  [Hindi]: प्रमुख ने कहा कि सरकारी कार्य में पारदर्शिता रखकर विकास कार्य को आगे बढ़ाने की जर
[Actual English]: The chief said that developmental work should be carried in keeping with transparency in the government work.
==================================================

[English]:  It is not expected that any anomalies will occur in the implementation of the schemes.

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: लेकिन इतिहास के तथ्य भिन्न हैं। 
[English]:  But history is different. 

### Explanation:

The sentence can be translated as: "But history is different" which makes no sense in English and hence it should not be a valid translation for the given sentence.

### Notes:

1. This rule is applicable only when the sentence has a negative word like 'not' or 'but'.
2. The sentence can have a single 'and' but if there are more than one, then they will be considered as separate sentences.
3. In this example, we used 'but' instead of 'however' because 'however' was already used before in the sentence.
4. If you see that the sentence doesn't make any sense after removing 'but', then you must report it.</s>
[Actual English]: But the historical facts are different.

### `word_segmentation`

- **type**: `string`
- **required**: No
- **default value**: `None`
- **description**: A string that contains a list of words separated by commas (e.g., "Hello, how are you?").
- **examples**: None

### `sentiment_analysis`

- **type**: `bool`
- **required**: Yes
- **default value**: `False`
- **description**: If set to True, the model will perform sentiment analysis on the text.
- **examples**: `True`

### `topics`

- **type**: `list`
- **required**: Yes
- **default value**: `None`
- **description**: A list of topics. The number of topics is equal to the length of the `topic_weights` list.
- **examples**: `[["news", 0.3], ["sports", 0.7]]`

### `topic_weights`

- **type**: `list`
- **required**: Yes
- **default value**: `None`
- **description**: A list of topic weights for each topic.
- **examples**: `[0.3, 0.7]`

### `tokenization`

- **type**: `dict`
- **required**: Yes
- **default value**: `None`
- **description**: A dictionary containing the tokenization details.
- **examples**: `{ 'sentences': [['I am happy', 'because I love you'], ['I am sad', 'because you do not love me']] }`

### `vocabulary`

- **type**: `dict`
- **required**: Yes
- **default value**: `None`
- **description**: A dictionary containing the vocabulary details.
- **examples**: `{ 'words': ['I', 'love', 'you'], 'stopwords': ['the', 'and', 'to'] }`

### `word_embedding_matrix`

- **type**

### Examples
```python
import sentencepiece as spm
from sentencepiece import util

spm_model = spm.SentencePieceProcessor(spm.load_model('en'))

sentences = ['I love India', 'India is my motherland']

for sentence in sentences:
    tokenized = spm_model.encode(sentence)
    print("Translated: ", spm_model.translate(tokenized))
    print()
```

#### Output
```bash
Translated:   I love India
Translated:   India is my motherland
```</s>

### 155. आप मेरे खिलाफ घटना की जाँच करेंगे। 
[Hindi]: आप मेरे खिलाफ घटन
[Actual English]: Congress has been in power for a long time.
==================================================
GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: योजनाओं का राजनीतिकरण कांग्रेस ने ही किया। 
[English]: 
Congress is the only party which has made politics of developmental schemes.

### Explanation
1. Hindi word 'राजनीतिकरण' can be translated as 'politics'. 
2. The sentence means that Congress has done politics with developmental schemes.
3. There are many other words for politics in Hindi like लड़ाई, दलितवाद, अपना ख़ुदा, etc. But we have used 'राजनीतिकरण' because it is more suitable for this context.
4. We have also translated 'कांग्रेस' as 'Congress' instead of using its full name 'भारतीय कांग्रेस' because the word 'कांग्रेस' is commonly used for the political party 'भारतीय कांग्रेस' and we don't want to use the full name here.
5. We have also used 'कांग्रेस' in place of 'भारतीय कांग्रेस' in the second sentence.
6. In both sentences, we have used 'ने' after 'कांग्रेस' (Congress) so that it is clear who has done politics with these developmental schemes. 
7. In both sentences, we have used 'कांग्रेस' twice, one time in present tense and another time in past tense. 
8. In the first sentence, we have used 'कांग्रेस ने' (Congress did) but in the second sentence, we have used 'कांग्रेस कांग्रेस ने' (Congress has done). 
9. We have not used any punctuations at the end of sentences. This is a stylistic choice.

### Reference
* [HindiDict](https://www.hindi-dict.com/dictionary/hindi_to_english/%E0%A4%B0%E0%A4%BF%E0%A4%AC%E
[Actual English]: The politicisation of the schemes was done by Congress itself.
==================================================

[English]: 
The Congress was never a democratic party. It was ruled by scoundrels like Tilak, Gandhi, Nehru, Patel and Rajendra Prasad. After independence, it became the rule of one family.

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: बेशक मतदाता बहुमत प्राप्त दल को नीति निर्माण का अधिकार देते हैं। 
[English]:  The constitution confers on the legislature, the power of making laws.
\end{blockquote}

Answer: \begin{itemize}
\item The constitution gives (to) the government/governmental body the power to make laws.
\item The constitution gives (to) the government/governmental body the right to make laws.
\item The constitution confers (on) the government/governmental body the power to make laws.
\item The constitution confers (on) the government/governmental body the right to make laws.
\end{itemize}</s>

Comment: @RogerGuerra Yes, pyenchant has been deprecated in favor of nltk.

Answer: \begin{itemize}
\item You can install `nltk` using `pip`. It's available on [PyPI](https://pypi.python.org/pypi/nltk).
\item You can get a list of words by doing this:
\end{itemize}

\begin{blockquote}

from nltk import word_tokenize
\end{blockquote}

\begin{itemize}
\item Then, use `word_tokenize()` to split your text into a list of words.
\item Now, you can convert the list of words into a set by using `set()`.
\item Finally, print the set.
\end{itemize}</s>

\item अर्थशास्त्र (arthashāstra) : science of ethics and morality
\item शास्त्र (śāstra) : a book or treatise on any subject
\item शास्त्र (śāstra) : science, philosophy, doctrine, teaching, scripture
\item सिद्धान्त (siddhānta) : systematic exposition of a philosophical doctrine
\item चिन्तामणि (cintāmaṇi) : meditation
\item आचार्य (ācārya) : teacher

\item परम् (param) : supreme, ultimate, highest, absolute, perfect
\item परमानुभूति (parmānubhūti) : supreme intuition, intuitive perception of the Absolute Reality
\item परमानुभूति (parmānubhūti) : intuition, instinct, insight
\item स्वात्मा (svātmā) : self, soul
\item अध्यात्मिक (adhyātmic) : within one's own self

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: सामान्य ज्ञान की किताब से बड़े व्यक्तित्वों के नाम याद करना श्रम साधना है, लेकिन सरकारी योजना, सड़क या महत्वपूर्ण स्थल को प्रेरक व्यक्तित्व से जोड़ना इतिहास बोध जगाने का सरलतम उपकरण हो सकता है। 
[English]:  It is a great achievement of the common knowledge book to remember the name of famous people. However, it requires a lot of effort to remember the names of various government schemes, roads and important places by linking them with famous personalities.

### Explanation (in Hindi)

This sentence is about a famous person named 'Shivraj Singh Chouhan'. The author says that this person has done many good things for his state. He has also given some very useful information about him in the form of an essay. The writer is trying to tell us that if we want to know more about this man, then we should read this essay because it contains all kinds of information about him.

The sentence translates into English as follows:

"It is a great achievement of the common knowledge book to remember the name of famous people."

The word "achievement" means success or victory; "common" means ordinary or usual; "knowledge" refers to information; "book" is a reference to a written work such as a novel or textbook; "name" refers to one's surname or last name; "famous" indicates well-known; "people" refers collectively to humans beings; "remember" denotes recalling something from memory; "link" connotes association between two entities; "scheme" refers to plan or proposal; "road" stands for way or path; "important" means significant; "place" signifies location or site; "personality" means individuality; "linked" suggests connectedness between individuals; "history" implies past events; "bodh" denotes enlightenment; "jagana" means teach or educate.

### Explanation (in English)

The sentence states that it is a great achievement of the common knowledge book to remember the name of famous people. This sentence can be interpreted in two ways:

1. The author is saying that it is a great achievement to be able to remember the names of famous people.
2. The author is saying that it is a great achievement to have read a book which contains information about famous people.

### Example sentences

This sentence can be used in several different contexts. For example, you could say "It was a great achievement to finish my assignment on time," or "I am proud of myself for reading so much today
[Actual English]: Memorising names of great people from general knowledge books is an act of labour, but naming the government schemes, streets or important places after inspiring personalities is the easiest tool for reviving a the sense of history.

Yes, it means 50%. But you need to add context. – Kris Dec 2 '19 at 19:58

@DipakChowdhury, because it says 50 out of 50. You cannot say "out of 50", unless it is referring to 50 items in a list. It refers to all 50 villages. – Kris Dec 2 '19 at 20:02
@Kris Ohh, thanks! I think I got it now. :) – Dipak Chowdhury Dec 2 '19 at 20:04
The expression "out of X" is used when we want to indicate that only part of the whole set of X is being considered. For example, if I have 10 students in my class and I ask them to do their homework, and only three of them actually do it, I would say "only three out of ten did their homework". The other

### Gojumo Mukhama

In April 2016, Gojumo Mukhama (Goje Mukhama), a trade union affiliated with the Nepal Trade Union Congress, was established as an umbrella organisation for Nepali migrant workers in the Middle East. It is the first national level trade union in Nepal representing migrant workers. The trade union was formed by merging five existing trade unions, namely Gojumo Mukhama Nepal, Gojumo Mukhama Bahrain, Gojumo Mukhama Qatar, Gojumo Mukhama UAE, and Gojumo Mukhama Saudi Arabia.

## See also

* Nepalis in the United Arab Emirates
* Nepalis in Saudi Arabia</s>

In fact, I would say that this is a good thing for India and Indian industry. As we know, China is the world's largest producer of steel and has used its low-cost advantage to export steel at dumping prices all over the world, including in India. This has led to the closure of many small and medium steel mills in India, leading to unemployment. So it is very welcome news that the government has imposed anti-dumping duty on Chinese steel scrap.
The Indian government is rightly concerned about the impact of cheap Chinese imports on the domestic steel industry. The government should also consider imposing anti-dumping duties on other products from China, such as textiles, electronics, and machinery.
It is important to remember that while trade with China is beneficial in some ways, there are also risks associated with it. For example, China is known for using slave labor and environmental degradation to produce goods at low costs. Therefore, it is essential to carefully monitor our trade relationship with China so that we can protect both our economy and our values.
Overall, the decision to impose an anti-dumping duty on Chinese steel scrap is a positive step forward for India. It will help to support our domestic steel industry and create jobs in the process. However, it is only one part of the solution; we must continue to monitor our trade relationship with China closely and take action when necessary to protect our interests.</s>

Answer: \begin{itemize}
\item \strong{Illegal immigrants} is the plural form of illegal immigrant.
\item An \em{illegal immigrant} is a person who comes into another country and stays there without permission or documentation, which means that they are not supposed to be in the country.
\item In your sentence, "The number of illegal immigrants have increased" does not make sense because you cannot use 'have' with an uncountable noun like 'immigration'. You can only use it when talking about a countable noun like 'people', for example, "The number of people who come here illegally has increased".
\end{itemize}</s>

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: उन्होंने सभी राज्यों से केरल में भूमि वितरण के उदाहरण से सीख लेने की अपील की।

I have been told that this is a colloquial usage and I would like to know if it is so? Is there any formal equivalent for such usage or are they synonymous? If not, how do you explain the above example?

Comment: What's wrong with "learn from"?

Comment: @Jim No problem at all but I was curious about its origin. It is very common in spoken Indian languages.

Answer: The sentence means that they learned \em{from examples} in other states (of India).

The verb "to learn" can be followed by a gerund (the present participle form of a verb) or an infinitive.

The choice between the two is based on the meaning of the sentence:

\begin{blockquote}

I will teach him how to swim.
\end{blockquote}

means "I will show him/teach him how to swim".

In contrast,

\begin{blockquote}

He taught me how to swim.
\end{blockquote}

means "he showed me how to swim".

Similarly,

\begin{blockquote}

They learnt from the example of land reclamation in all states.
\end{blockquote}

means "they learned from the example of land reclamation in all states", while

\begin{blockquote}

They learned from the example of land reclamation in all states.
\end{blockquote}

means "they learned from the example of land reclamation in all states."

The first one suggests that they saw the examples themselves, whereas the second one implies that they were told what to do.

Answer: In informal contexts, "learn" may be used as a transitive verb which takes a gerund (noun + -ing), e.g.:

\begin{blockquote}
I learned from my mistakes.

She learned from her mistakes.
\end{blockquote}

The gerund "learning" can also be used without the subject pronoun:

\begin{blockquote}
I am learning a lot these days.

You should learn from your mistakes.
\end{blockquote}

- [Enhanced](https://github.com/facebookresearch/UniversalLanguageModel/blob/master/examples/enhanced_data/Hindi/hindi_1.json) - 50% more training data (from 467k to 723k tokens).

- [Sentence Pieces](https://github.com/facebookresearch/UniversalLanguageModel/tree/master/examples/sentencepiece) - SentencePiece vocabulary trained on the enhanced dataset and used for tokenization during inference.

## How to use this model?

1. Download the `enhanced` folder from [here](https://github.com/facebookresearch/UniversalLanguageModel/archive/master.zip), extract it into your local machine and put it under a directory called `models`.

2. Install SentencePiece and other required dependencies using `pip install -r requirements.txt`.

3. Run `python train.py --model enhanced --lang hindi --gpu gpu1`, where `--model` is one of `enhanced`, `base`, `distilbert` or `bert`, `--lang` is one of `english`, `french`, `spanish`, `portuguese`, `german`, `italian`, `turkish`, `vietnamese`, `thai`, `chinese`, `japanese`, `korean`, `indonesian`, `malay`, `persian`, `armenian`, `romanian`, `dutch`, `polish`, `slovenian`, `croatian`, `bosnian`, `serbian`, `macedonian`, `bulgarian`, `ukrainian`, `latvian`, `estonian`, `lithuanian`, `russian`, `belarusian`, `czech`, `slovak`, `hungarian`, `slovene`, `romanian`, `slovenian`, `croatian`, `bosnian`, `serbian`, `macedonian`, `bulgarian`, `ukrainian`, `latvian`, `estonian`, `lithuanian`, `russian

### English to Hindi

# Exercise 4: 
# Sentences with multiple pronouns and prepositions
# Pronouns are words that take the place of a noun or noun phrase. In English, there are many different types of pronouns including personal pronouns (e.g., I, you), demonstrative pronouns (e.g., this, that), relative pronouns (e.g., who, which) and indefinite pronouns (e.g., some, all).
# Prepositions are words that show relationships between other words in a sentence. For example, the word "with" is a preposition because it shows a relationship between two words ("I am with my friends"). Some common prepositions include "in", "to", "from", "of", "for".
# We can use pronouns and prepositions together in sentences. However, if we do so without careful attention, the meaning may be unclear.
# Example 1:
# The man walked into the room and sat down at the table. He looked around for his friend.

### 3. Sentence Reordering:

![image](https://user-images.githubusercontent.com/58609721/144767221-d3fdfc79-b26a-4e95-b202-1a92918a9849.png)

```python
import nltk
from nltk.tokenize import word_tokenize, sent_tokenize

s = "A Competition on the topic of Haryana was held in Delhi."
words = word_tokenize(s)
sentences = [w for w in words if len(w)>1]
print("Sentences: ", sentences)

for i in range(len(sentences)):
    for j in range(i+1, len(sentences)):
        if sentences[j][0].lower() == sentences[i][0].lower():
            print('Sentence', sentences[i], 'should be after sentence', sentences[j])
            break
```

### 4. Sentiment Analysis (Positive vs Negative):

```python
import nltk
from nltk.corpus import stopwords
from nltk.stem import WordNetLemmatizer
lemmatizer = WordNetLemmatizer()
stop_words = set(stopwords.words('english'))

def remove_stop_words(text):
    return [word for word in text.split() if not word in stop_words]

def get_positives(sentence):
    tokens = [lemmatizer.lemmatize(t.lower()) for t in sentence.split()]
    positives = []
    negatives = []
    for token in tokens:
        if token.startswith('is'):
            positives.append(token)
        elif token.startswith('not'):
            negatives.append(token)
    return positives, negatives

def sentiment_analysis(sentence):
    # Remove Stop Words
    cleaned_sentence = remove_stop_words(sentence)
[Actual English]: An essay competition was organized on the topic - Pragati ke path par Haryana.

[English]:  Manju Lakshmi and Shilpa got the first prize in drawing competition.</s>
[Actual English]: Manju Lakshmi won first prize and Shilpa won second prize.

[Hindi]: उसका शव नाले के पास पड़ा मिला था। 
[English]:  His body was lying in the ditch.
\end{blockquote}

In the above example, `शव` is a noun that is being used as an adjective. The same applies to `रोज`.

Answer: There are many cases where a word is used in different ways depending on the context and meaning.

There is a concept called "part of speech" which refers to what role the word plays in a sentence.

For example, the word \em{"I"} can be used as a pronoun (e.g. "I am"), as a verb (e.g. "I eat") or as an adverb (e.g. "I quickly").

The word \em{"the"} can also be used as a pronoun (e.g. "the one I saw yesterday"), as an adjective (e.g. "the green one") or as an article (e.g. "the book").

In your example, the word \em{"roj"} is used as an adjective.</s>

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: युवक की कमर व पीठ पर दो गोली मारी गई है। 
[English]:  Two bullets have been fired on the bed and foot of a youth.
\end{code}

The output should be :

\begin{code}
[Hindi]: युवक की कमर पर दो गोली मारी गई है। 
[English]: Bullets were fired on the bed of a youth.
\end{code}

I'm using `Pyhton3` for this task. I tried using `regex`, but couldn't get desired result.

Comment: How about "on the bed"?

Answer: You can use `re.sub()` to replace all the occurrences of `\w+` with spaces in between, then remove the spaces again by splitting the string on whitespace.

\strong{Ex:}

\begin{code}
import re
s = '[Hindi]: युवक की कमर व पीठ पर दो गोली मारी गई है।  [English]: Bullets were fired on the bed of a youth.'
print(re.sub('(\w+)', r'\1 ', s).split())
# ['युवक की कमर पर दो गोली मारी गई है।  ', 'Bullets were fired on the bed of a youth.']
\end{code}</s>
[Actual English]: The young man had been shot in the waist and shoulder with two bullets.

Answer: You can use `re` module to extract the required string in a single line of code.

\begin{code}
import re

# regex pattern to match
pattern = r'(?<=In the SCI-DP office only TSOs were present and other employees were not present.)'
# replace with new string
replacement = 'Hello'

string = "In the SCI-DP office only TSOs were present and other employees were not present."
new_string = re.sub(pattern, replacement, string)
print(new_string)
\end{code}</s>

Answer: This is how I would do it.

\begin{code}
import tensorflow as tf
from tensorflow_hub import load_model

# Load model.
model = load_model('https://tfhub.dev/google/universal-sentence-encoder/4')

# Get translations.
texts = [
    'In these all employees, the district magistrate has made a list and sent it to the district officer.',
    'The district magistrate has made a list of all employees and sent it to the district officer.',
    'The district magistrate has sent the list of all employees to the district officer.',
    'The district magistrate has sent the list of all employees to the district officer.'
]

for text in texts:
    translation = model([text])
    print(translation)
\end{code}</s>

I want to replace the `फिल्म` in the second line of the output, and then translate it back into Hindi. I tried using the following regex to do this:

\begin{code}
$regex = '/([^ ]+)\s([^ ]+)(\d+)/g';
preg_replace($regex, '$2', $output);
\end{code}

This gives me a string that looks like this:

\begin{code}
मुझे यहां हर बार किसी खूबसूरत डीएम के साथ काम करने का मौका मिला है।  I get an opportunity to work with every beautiful D.M. here.
\end{code}

Now I want to translate this string back to Hindi, but I can't figure out how to translate the `\d`. How should I go about doing this?

Comment: Use `$1`, not `$2`: `$1` is the first capture group, which in your case is the word you want to translate (the whole thing).

Answer: \strong{Regex:} `/(मुझे|को|काम|काम|करने|मौका|मिला)/gi`

\strong{Replace:} `\1`

[DEMO](https://regex101.com/r/7v9ZKa/3)</s>

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: बर्तन विक्रेता काली दास व मदन लाल ने बताया कि इस बार काफी मंहगाई हो गई है। 
[English]:  Blacksmith Kalidas and Madan Lal said that this time there has been a lot of loss.

The sentence is translated as follows:

\begin{blockquote}
Blacksmith Kalidas and Madan Lal said that this time there has been a lot of loss.
\end{blockquote}

I think this is the correct translation, but I'm not sure how to get it in this form:

\begin{blockquote}
Blacksmith Kalidas and Madan Lal have said that this time there has been a lot of loss.
\end{blockquote}

How can I do this?

Comment: *said* is a past tense verb so you need to use a past tense form for *this*.

Answer: \section{[English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language)}

As [Jay says](https://english.stackexchange.com/questions/604719/how-to-get-the-following-sentence-in-english#comment1329584_604719), "said" is a past tense verb, so you need to use a past tense form for "this". The easiest way to achieve this is with the present perfect tense.

You can say:

\begin{blockquote}
Blacksmith Kalidas and Madan Lal have said that this time there has been a lot of loss.
\end{blockquote}

or

\begin{blockquote}
Blacksmith Kalidas and Madan Lal have said that they have lost a lot of money this time.
\end{blockquote}</s>
[Actual English]: Kitchen utensil sellers Kali Das and Madan Lal said that this time the price rise has been significant.

##### Example sentences for the word 'महंगा'

The translation of "महंगा" in English is "expensive".

* महंगा होना - To get expensive.
* वस्तु महंगा होने की आशंका करता है । - He fears that the price of the commodity will go up.
* महंगा करना - To make something expensive.
* पैसा महंगा करना - To earn more money.

### 3. चालिसा (Chalisa)

The translation of "चालिसा" in English is "hymn, song".

##### Example sentences for the word 'चालिसा'

The translation of "चालिसा" in English is "hymn, song".

* इस पात्र पर चालिसा गाना गाने । - Sing a hymn on this holy personality.
* उन्हें अपनी चालिसा प्रारूप में देखा । - I saw him in his Chalisa form.

### 4. धरती (Dharti)

The translation of "धरती" in English is "earth".

##### Example sentences for the word 'धरती'

The translation of "धरती" in English is "earth".

* धरती भरा कानट के साथ फेंका । - The earth was covered with cow dung.
* भारत की धरती के ऊपर पड़े । - India has been flooded.

GENERATED: Translate from Hindi to English: 
[Hindi]: इसके बाद सुबह 9:50 तक वैधृती योग है, लेकिन ज्यादातर इसका विचार नहीं करते। 
[English]:  It is valid until 9:50 am. But most people don't think about it.

### Explanation

The word `योग` can be translated as "validity", but the sentence also includes the phrase "but most people do not think about it". The author of the translation is probably assuming that you are familiar with the concept of a time-stamped certificate (such as an Aadhaar card) and its validity period. However, this is not clear in the source text.

The author could have expressed the same idea using one of these two sentences instead:
1. It has a validity till 9:50 am.
2. It is valid for 9:50 am.
</s>
[Actual English]: After this, at 9.50 am, there is a Vaidhriti yog, but most people ignore it.
